< Review>
My son is an incoming freshman and I just went to the campus for the first time to drop him off for orientation.  I can't possibly say enough good things about Santa Clara University.  Over the last 2 years, we have traveled to over 20 college campuses all across the United States and Santa Clara is among the best in the country.  The campus is absolutely beautiful and surrounded by a wonderful community.  For parents, Santa Clara provided security that your child (even though an adult) will have a safe and quality environment to grow and lean in.  Not a Catholic, but of the Christian faith, I have been very impressed with the Jesuit way of higher education.  I have only taken the time to write 3 or 4 on-line reviews in my life, but I can honestly say that I am so proud to be a Santa Clara parent!  Go Broncos!
Marc Mitzner</Review>

(Translated by Google) Santa Clara University (also referred to as Santa Clara) is a private Jesuit university in Santa Clara, California. There are 5,499 full-time students and 3,130 postgraduate students. Founded in 1851 AD, Santa Clara University is the oldest institution of higher education in California and the West Coast of the United States, and has remained in its original location for 169 years. The university campus is surrounded by the historic mission of Santa Clara de Assis, dating back to 1776 AD. The campus reflects the architectural style of the university's mission, and provides a good early example of the mission to revive architecture. The university is classified as a "doctoral / professional" university, in the Carnegie ranking.

<rating>3< /rating>< Text>
First 'not so good' experience at El Pollo Loco on El Cajon Blvd. I've been here a few times where overall the experience was ok. Unfortunately this time the customer service, from the general manager was very unfriendly. The tostada salad I had was good with some pieces of very dry and overcooked chicken and the tostada was very cold. I understand that it's a salad and I'm aware that the tostada is supposed to be room temperature. But for it to be COLD and for the GM's demeanor to be 'welp, that's just how it is' - is rude. I had to go back and forth with her a few times to give me a fresh warm tostada. Which she just handed to me with the cold tostada and a get-out-of-my-face look. The overall experience wasn't that bad but in comparison to the one I usually go to in Mission Valley, it is. Still love El Pollo Loco just bad customer service here.</Text>

<Text>This is a very nice park for what it is, a smaller neighborhood park.  As mentioned by someone else it is small but I think the philosophy of the park is to provide a fun space with a variety of stimuli.  If you need wide open space, the nearby Great Park will fit the bill.  This park is great for the residents with a pool (probably for residents only) but also a performing arts space, gallery space and studio (currently occupied by building info and layouts but the long term plan is to display art), and various play/sports.  There are two half court basketball courts (separate sides of the park), mini ampitheatre, variety of play structures, tetherball, walking paths, all in all a pretty cool place.<//Text><pics>None<//pics><Response>None<//Response><gmapID>0x80dcc2c7bd9e029b:0x12ecd071654729f4<//gmapID></record>

<name>Kimberly</name>< rating>
1< /rating>
< review>
My friend wanted me to try this place.   I love sushi...but it must be cooked...I cannot eat raw fish..the texture makes me gag...sorry...

I agreed to come...

When you walk in...you are greeted right away...

Upon entering there is a little chinese food buffet with egg rolls...general chicken...salt and pepper shrimp...rice...chow mein...

If you sit at the bar and order the all you can eat...this is included.

The staff were very attractive...the rolls came out fast.

The reason my review only gets 1 star...the food on the buffet was cold...there is no menu...that you can look at and see what can be ordered in a roll that is cooked.

I have been to Aji sushi and loved it...that's where I wanted to go...but he wanted to come here.

You sit at a bar area and can pick sushi up from these little boats...the boats are so darn cute...the only problem..if you do not know what is on or in the roll..how does one know if they like it...well..I tried about 3 different rolls and did not like any of them...

So I shared some fried shrimp..that was good...and the salt and pepper shrimp were good...and 2 sesame balls.

I will not come back...I would have liked it more if there was a menu that you can read from and order like other places...oh well...it was an experience...but I told him..that place is a no.<//review>

< text>
Pretty good! Cool that they have Chinese style buffet along with the sushi. They do sashimi which is key to getting a good value at any ayce sushi place.

I feel that they should have menus at the tables though. They don't really do that. You just have to know or ask or revert to this chalkboard where they only list a few of the items they do. Kinda odd. Especially since different places call different rolls by different names. It's not all universal and this definitely caused a little bit of confusion when ordering. They have a menu but only at the front and they use it for to go orders but it's also technically what you can order during buffet. Strange!

Grilled salmon was impressively good. Everything else was pretty much as expected. Good! Might come back if I'm in the area but I wouldn't make the drive just for this place.<//text>

BEBACK rating- most likely

It‚Äôs been a long time between this visit and the last time I was here. I‚Äôm glad it is still open.

Anyway, the bad:
1. I had the miso soup and the egg drop soup that they have at the side of the main area. The miso was about as good as any other Japanese restaurant but the egg drop soup was bland. In fact, it seemed like I was eating thickened water.

2. I was very disappointed when I watched an employee serve himself food on a used plate instead of a new one. The serving spoon he used touched the plate which had leftover whatever.

People! At a buffet, use a new plate! No one wants to use a serving spoon that may have your saliva on it. Well, maybe it‚Äôs ok at home when eating with your family, I guess.

Here‚Äôs the good:

1. The tuna collar is still excellent. If you don‚Äôt know, the collar is usually where you‚Äôll get the best flavor of the tuna.

2. I‚Äôm glad they still have the deep fried oysters and soft shell crab. We had the oysters, flavorful, although I prefer larger pieces that explode with the oyster juice when you bite it- like at your small fish and chips joints.

3. The sushi boats are entertaining and practical since you can actually see what your choosing instead of looking at a picture of it on a menu.

4. Lastly, the bussers and water servers were on the ball and came by often to remove dishes and to make sure our water and tea was not empty.

All in all, I will continue to recommend this restaurant despite the no-no by the employee.<//Review>

This place has gone downhill in the past 6 months to a year. The hours have changed and the quality of sushi has gotten worse. I had no idea of their hours changing and went to lunch today at 1:30. Instead of telling me they weren't accepting anyone coming in anymore they sat me and my family and told us they were closing at 2 pm. The sushi they served was all filled with artificial crab and heavy mayo, nothing raw.

Promptly at 2 pm they started shutting down and taking everything out so there wasn't any food left. Why not just tell your customer you're not accepting anyone after 1:30 because you're switching over for the dinner service instead of taking all the food out and shutting down? We were told we could finish what we had gotten but they were closing. Their hours used to be open until 3 pm for lunch and I had no idea they had changed this.

It cost 3 people 70 bucks for 30 minutes of being able to eat there and the food wasn't even good. We were essentially rushed out the door too. I won't be going here again and I think the ownership has changed hands and the new owners keep making things worse. Sushi quality has gone down the drain and the last time I went a few months ago they had changed their hours from stopping lunch 3 pm and opening at 4 pm to stopping lunch at 2 pm and opening at 5 pm for dinner.

Next time when you change your hours like this you should make it really well known to your customers, and instead of sitting people 30 minutes before you close to take their money anyways tell them you are closing in 30 minutes and not accepting customers until dinner service.< /review>

<Time>1545027466234<//Time><user_id>102127325548403576700<//user_id>< text>
Overall it's your basic quality buffet.
Pros: variety of sushi rolls, made to order sashimi and specialty items.  Best fresh made sesame balls I've ever tasted.  Very attentive when you line up to pick off the sushi line on what you need. There's also a Chinese food area which was your standard  fruit area to Chow mien to stir fry  and deep fry foods.
Cons: This could have been a one time experience, but all the sushi quality taste like just thawed frozen fish.  Some still tasted like they had ice in the middle of them.  They were bland. All the fish actually tasted the same, from salmon (which should be buttery) to tuna.
If you're looking for variety of sushi with quality, there's other all you can eat sushi at the same price, but better quality.< /text>

<rate>4<//rate><review>All-you-can-eat sushi is always a little daunting. What's the quality like? Do they change it out often enough? Are there any items of note or is it just the cheap stuff?

The good news with Fuji is that it's definitely worth the trip. The quality is good,  and there are some real surprises, like their salmon sashimi and dragon roll. They have a rotating selection of sushi boat stuff BUT you can also special order if you don't see what you want.

<Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
Okay, I had to write a review to counter all the people saying super negative things about this place. Don't listen to all the negative comments. No, this is not the restaurant run by Jiro, but it is perfectly acceptable. It is a great price for good food. I ride my bike over to this place with my little daughter all the time. The service is good, sometimes slow when it is busy, but damn be patient, the place is always packed (and for a good reason). And to the people complaining about the service... you probably are just too shy to go to the sushi bar and ask for something; that is your fault no theirs.

This is not a place to eat if you are in a hurry or if you expect to have some waiter brown nose you so you can feel good about yourself.

Price: Perfect
Food: Good
Service: Good</Review>

< Text>
They have all you can eat sushi, which is nice. The sushi is not great quality fish, which is not so nice, and maybe even a little worrying, though I have not gotten sick yet after eating here probably 10 times or so (knock on wood). The rolls are okay, but I tend to stick with the nigiri. If you are adventurous, you can get endless plates of oysters - I am even less trusting of the quality here, but again, never got sick. Wait times aren't bad if you come on slow nights, but Friday night can take a while. They have cooked Chinese food, fruit, and an ice cream machine, but if you eat that, why did you go to an all-you-can-eat sushi place?<//Text>

<Text>I have been going to Fuji since they were located in Davis since 2006ish. I use to wait line an hour before they opened to get a spot. When they initially opened the Elk Grove location I felt that the service and quality of the food had gone down, BUT I was craving sushi and soft shell crab and decided to give them another try.

THE QUALITY OF THE SASHIMI, SUSHI AND FOOD was great! üëçüèΩüç£üç§ü¶êü¶Äüêôü•¢It's what I remembered I loved about Fuji when I first started going in college.

Service: was VERY FAST and friendly. You can go up to the counter and order sashimi, sushi rolls, Hand rolls, seared tuna/salmon, soft shell crab, tuna collar, etc... On the other side they have a self serve buffet with soup, rice, chow mein, chicken, shrimp, veggies, dessert, etc... The food if very fresh and made to order so you don't have to worry about whether or not the food has been sitting there for a while.  They rotate it quickly.  They can also customize your roll if you want to add or subtract anything from it.

I would HIGHLY RECCOMEND this place and its a great place to go with a group of friends or family.< /Text>< pics>

<review>This is mostly a sushi buffet....

I say this because, although there are some side dishes, ie., chicken wings, veggie dishes, soup, the customers are here for the sushi which is average at best, in my opinion. The tuna was somewhat dry in flavor and the cooked shrimp chewy.

The sushi is served on little boats that float by tables at the sushi bar.  You can imagine that the bar is filled up quickly.

Salmon, salmon eggs, clam sushi are scarce unless you place an order, which necessitates you stand in a long line.

The place opens at 11 but there's a long line before the door opens giving credence of the popularity of this establishment.

My biggest gripe was the rude waiters and a member of our family not being able to sit with us unless she paid the $17.50 lunch admission.

We did eat our money's worth, stood in line for special orders, and getting bumped with the packed room of other competitive eaters/diners.

Didn't have to leave a tip because we paid to include our family member to be with us instead of sitting outside by herself.  Not my favorite of places....<//review>< pictures>

I honestly don't understand why this place is so popular.  I have never been to a buffet where they had you pay before they seat you. This place has changed since I was here last time (couple years ago). There are no more lines out the door, but they did have several people eating here for a weekday lunch. <Time>1544768616588< /Time>< userid>
105990278169856318164</userid>
<resp>None</resp><username>Lorrayne G<//username><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
My 14 year old daughter loves sushi and i like sushi so long as it does not contain raw fish so shrimp and crab or deep fried rolls. I had seen a line of people waiting for the restaurant to open for dinner many times while on my way to Wal-Mart and many Asian people in that line so i decided we should try it. It was busy on a Thursday night.  We sat at the sushi bar and it was so cool to have the little boats go around with a variety of small plates for you to grab. They also had rolls you could order and shrimp soft shell blue crab and mixed vegetable tempura which were excellent. And there was a Chinese food section with chow mein fried rice honey walnut style shrimp spicy orange chicken teriyaki chicken green bean shrimp brandy fried chicken wings and gyoza. The Chinese food rated a solid B. However the vegetarian hot and sour soup was excellent and it is my favorite soup and i am very picky about the quality of the soup. Also the sunamono cucumber salad was amazing. There is also fresh fruit and dessert. I tried several different sushi plates. Some were really good others just not my cup of tea. However i left absolutely stuffed. My daughter loved it too. We are going to take my pescatarian  (only eats sea food) niece here next month. It was $50 for two of us so a bit on the pricey side but the selection was quite large and the quality was great so it was worth the money. If you want to sample a variety of sushi this is definitely the way to go.<//review>

This place is so wonderful. It's definitely a little pricey but worth every dime. My boyfriend, son, my mom and I ate quite a bit of stuff. We had the caterpillar, tiger, California, and golden rolls; shrimp and vegetables tampura; teriyaki chicken; egg rolls; chicken goyza; honey shrimp; chow mein; fried rice; chicken wings; and some amazing cakes that were orange and coffee flavoured. The only thing that wasn't liked was the teriyaki chicken and that was my son who didn't like it, I thought it had the perfect amount of sweet flavor. I would recommend this restaurant to anyone because their menu is very diverse and it doesn't even smell super fishy like some sushi restaurants do. However! My boyfriend did say that the men's bathroom was dirty which is why I'm giving them a 4 star rating instead of 5. Otherwise 10/10 and would eat there again any time I'm in Elk Grove.<//review>

<Rate>5< /Rate><review>i have came here many times and i would like to update my review.

i came here over the weekend on a saturday morning around 11 15am. we were lucky that day wasn't too crowded or busy. we didn't have to wait and went straight in and got seated in a table for 5.

for the line situation it is usually packed. i mean no joke be there 30 mins early to get in line fore they open because there are usually people lingering waiting for it to open for lunch or dinner. if you want to sit near the sushi bar then at east 30 mins ahead of time. if just tables then 15 mins ahead before opening time.

as soon as you get seated you are free to get what ever you want from the sushi boat or the food on display hear the ends of the sushi boats. they usually have lots of rolls already made and you can just grab them. sometimes they have the sushi chefs shouting out sashimi or sear sashimi spicy or non spicy with special sauces in them, or deep fried tempura shrimp, oysters or soft shell crab or mix tempura with a little bit of everything. you can always order with them too. just don't be shy to shout or say it in a loud voice because its loud inside and they might not be able hear you.

some tips for ordering through the busy sushi chef,
1. speak loud so they can hear you
2. when you order the sashimi make sure you tell them what you want. theres salmon, tuna, saba, hamachi, shrimp, octopus, and etc.
3. when you order their sashimi, tell them the size of it. a small can feed 2 people. med can feed 3 to 4. large can feed 4 to 6.
4. they also have seared sashimi which can be spicy or non spicy due to request. also tell them the size and which fish. i had the spicy pepper fin and omg it was amazing!
5. you can order the fried oyster, shrimp, soft shel crab or a mix of it all. just say mix tempura if you want a little bit of everything to discover what you favorite is.
6. also the grilled hamachi kama which is fish neck. it has a large bone with meat on the side and its amazing!
7. they also have raw oyster half shell too.
8. they also carry tobiko which is fish caviar and topped with a quail egg which is raw too, this is perfect for instagraming hehe.
9. also they have hand rolls too, some famous hand rolls is called the spider hand roll, one of my favorite creations from me is the avocado and tobiko which is amazing, with the smooth creamy texture of avocado with the popping crisp fish eggs.
10. also they have custom sushi rolls, just tell them what you want inside and they will make it for you.

the service is always pretty good. they will come by your table and clear your empty plates. they also refill your water often so thats a plus. the layout of the inside is big so its great for large parties. also there are lots of parking so parking isn't a issue. also if your not a fan of raw sushi, don't worry they have cook sushi rolls too. also they have a chinese hot food section with chow mien, fried rice, to egg rolls, and mixed vegetables stir fry, pot stickers, egg rolls, and teriyaki chicken sticks to desserts and fresh fruits. overall its a amazing place to come here and try it. bring your first time relatives to come here and usually it will impress them. if you like my review don't forget to add or follow me and read some more. thanks for reading!</review><time>1528855961168</time></record></dataset><record>
